                        cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Reversible Lithium Storage at Highly Populated Vacant Sites in an Amorphous Vanadium Pentoxide Electrode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chae, Oh B.; Kim, Jisun; Park, Inchul; Jeong, Hyejeong; Ku, Jun H.; Ryu, Ji Heon; Kang, Kisuk; Oh, Seung M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">26</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">20</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5874-5881</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0897-4756</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A V pentoxide electrode is prepd. in the amorphous form (a-V2O5), and its electrode performances are compared to those for its cryst. counterpart (c-V2O5).  The a-V2O5 electrode outperforms c-V2O5 in several ways.  First, it is free from irreversible phase transitions and Li trapping, which evolve in c-V2O5, probably due to the lack of interactions between the inserted Li+ ions/electrons and V2O5 matrix.  Second, the absence of Li trapping allows a reversible capacity amounting to &gt;600 mA-h g-1, which is larger than that given by c-V2O5.  Third, it shows an excellent rate property.  The notably high reversible capacity and rate capability seem to be due to Li storage at vacant sites that are ill-defined but numerous in a-V2O5, which Li+ ions can easily access.  However, irreversible capacity of a-V2O5 is appreciable in the 1st cycle due to a parasitic Li reaction with surface hydroxyl groups.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The chem. diffusion coeffs. of lithium ion (DLi+) in Li1 + xVPO4F (0 ≤ x ≤ 2) between 3.0 and 0.01 V are systematically analyzed by cyclic voltammetry (CV), electrochem. impedance spectroscopy (EIS), and galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique (GITT). And a Na0.3MoO2//Na0.8Ni0.4Ti0.6O2 full intercalation-type sodium-ion cell is fabricated and it displays an excellent cycling stability.  These results indicate that molybdenum-based oxide is a promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref45" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1149/2.0211711jes"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Taleghani, S.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Study on the Effect of Porosity and Particles Size Distribution on Li-Ion Battery Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Taleghani, Sara Taslimi; Marcos, Bernard; Zaghib, Karim; Lantagne, Gaetan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Electrochemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A pseudo two-dimensional model (P2D) is presented that describes the effect of the structural properties of the pos. electrode on Li-ion cell performance during discharge.  The validation of the mono-modal model was done by using Doyle's expt. and results [C.M. Doyle, University of California, Berkeley (1995)].  A large increase or decrease in the porosity beyond a specific value led to a sharp change in the cell voltage curve and lower cell capacities.  The max. specific energy was obtained in the porosity range of 0.55, while the specific power still had a high value.  Furthermore, different particle size distribution models, including mono-modal, bi-modal and 3-particle models, were compared to each other.  The mono-modal model was the ideal state with the lowest total polarization.  The bi-modal and 3-particle models approached this ideal state when the vol. fraction of the smallest particles in their structures increased.  This structural arrangement in these models led to more uniform local c.d. distribution profiles resulting in a greater decrease in cell polarization.  Different discharge current densities were applied to different particle size distribution models, and the results showed that the particle size distribution has a greater effect at higher discharge current densities.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref46" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1038/s41598-017-16711-9"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, Y.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ryu, K.-S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Study of the lithium diffusion properties and high rate performance of TiNb6O17 as an anode in lithium secondary battery</span>. <i>Sci.     </div><div class="casAbstract">TiNb6O17 and TiNb2O7 were synthesized using a solid-state method.  The techniques were used to assess the electrochemical performance and lithium diffusion kinetics of TiNb6O17 related to the unit cell volume with TiNb2O7.  The charge-discharge curves and cyclic voltammetry revealed TiNb6O17 to have a similar redox potential to TiNb2O7 as well as a high discharge capacity.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Potentiostatic intermittent titrn. technique (PITT) and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy (EIS) were studied as methods to det. solid phase chem. diffusion coeff. (D) and electronic d. of states (DOS).  These techniques were then applied to Ir oxide (IrOx) and Ir-Ta oxide (IrTaOx) thin films prepd. by sputter deposition.  The expts., performed in 1M propionic acid between -0.2 and 0.8 V vs. Ag/AgCl, showed effects of interfacial side reactions, whose contribution to the electrochem. response could be identified and cor. for in the case of PITT as well as EIS. EIS indicated an anomalous diffusion mechanism, and D is in the 10-11-10-10 cm2/s range for IrOx and IrTaOx.  Both PITT and EIS showed that the intercalated charge as a function of potential exhibits a shape that resembles the theor. DOS of cryst. Ir oxide, esp. for IrTaOx.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Better Cycling Performances of Bulk Sb in Na-Ion Batteries Compared to Li-Ion Systems: An Unexpected Electrochemical Mechanism</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Darwiche, Ali; Marino, Cyril; Sougrati, Moulay T.; Fraisse, Bernard; Stievano, Lorenzo; Monconduit, Laure</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">134</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">51</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">20805-20811</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pure micrometric antimony can be successfully used as neg. electrode material in Na-ion batteries, sustaining a capacity close to 600 mAh g-1 at a high rate with a Coulombic efficiency of 99 over 160 cycles, an extremely high capacity compared to any other compd. tested against both Li and Na.  The reaction mechanism with Na does not simply go through the alloying mechanism obsd. for Li where the intermediate species are those expected from the phase diagram.  In the case of Na, the intermediate phases are mostly amorphous and could not be precisely identified.  Surprisingly, it is evidenced that a competition takes place at the end of the discharge of the Sb/Na cell between the formation of the hexagonal and the cubic polymorphs of Na3Sb, the last being described in the literature as unstable at atm. pressure and only synthesized under high pressure (1-9 GPa).  In addn., fluoroethylene carbonate added to the electrolyte combined with an appropriate electrode formulation based on CM-cellulose, carbon black, and vapor ground carbon fibers seems to be determinant in the excellent performances of this material.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript" nonce="93188881ef5754b8-SJC">window.refViewer={'ref1':['cit1'],'ref2':['cit2'],'ref3':['cit3'],'ref4':['cit4'],'ref5':['cit5'],'ref6':['cit6'],'ref7':['cit7'],'ref8':['cit8'],'ref9':['cit9'],'ref10':['cit10'],'ref11':['cit11'],'ref12':['cit12'],'ref13':['cit13'],'ref14':['cit14'],'ref15':['cit15'],'ref16':['cit16'],'ref17':['cit17'],'ref18':['cit18'],'ref19':['cit19'],'ref20':['cit20'],'ref21':['cit21'],'ref22':['cit22'],'ref23':['cit23'],'ref24':['cit24'],'ref25':['cit25'],'ref26':['cit26'],'ref27':['cit27'],'ref28':['cit28'],'ref29':['cit29'],'ref30':['cit30'],'ref31':['cit31'],'ref32':['cit32'],'ref33':['cit33'],'ref34':['cit34'],'ref35':['cit35'],'ref36':['cit36'],'ref37':['cit37'],'ref38':['cit38'],'ref39':['cit39'],'ref40':['cit40'],'ref41':['cit41'],'ref42':['cit42'],'ref43':['cit43'],'ref44':['cit44'],'ref45':['cit45'],'ref46':['cit46'],'ref47':['cit47'],'ref48':['cit48'],'ref49':['cit49'],'ref50':['cit50']}</script><div class="articleCitedByDropzone" data-pb-dropzone="articleCitedByDropzone"><div class="cited-by"><div class="article_content-header cited-content_header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div tabindex="0" class="article_content-title"><h2 id="citeThis">Cited By</h2><div class="article__copy"> <button class="article__copy__btn"><i aria-hidden="true" class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><div class="cited-by__content"><div class="sciteMetricsDropzone">

            This article references
            50 other publications.
        </p><ol id="rightTab-references" class="useLabel"><li id="rightTab-ref1"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref1" class="rightTabRefNumLink">1</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit1" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms7865"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hwang, J.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oh, S.-M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Myung, S.-T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chung, K. Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Belharouak, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.-K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Radially aligned hierarchical columnar structure as a cathode material for high energy density sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Nat. Commun.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>6</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">6865</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/ncomms7865</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Radially aligned hierarchical columnar structure as a cathode material for high energy density sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Oh, Seung-Min; Myung, Seung-Taek; Chung, Kyung Yoon; Belharouak, Ilias; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6865</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NCAOBW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2041-1723</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Delivery of high capacity with good retention is a challenge in developing cathodes for rechargeable sodium-ion batteries.  Here we present a radially aligned hierarchical columnar structure in spherical particles with varied chem. compn. from the inner end (Na[Ni0.75Co0.02Mn0.23]O2) to the outer end (Na[Ni0.58Co0.06Mn0.36]O2) of the structure.  With this cathode material, we show that an electrochem. reaction based on Ni2+/3+/4+ is readily available to deliver a discharge capacity of 157 mAh (g-oxide)-1 (15 mA g-1), a capacity retention of 80% (125 mAh g-1) during 300 cycles in combination with a hard carbon anode, and a rate capability of 132.6 mAh g-1 (1,500 mA g-1, 10 C-rate).  The cathode also exhibits good temp. performance even at -20°C.  These results originate from rather unique chem. of the cathode material, which enables the Ni redox reaction and minimizes the surface area contacting corrosive electrolyte.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms15888"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bie, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dixon, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bramnik, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fauth, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ehrenberg, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium vanadium titanium phosphate electrode for symmetric sodium-ion batteries with high power and long lifespan</span>. <i>Nat. Commun.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>8</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">15888</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/ncomms15888</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium vanadium titanium phosphate electrode for symmetric sodium-ion batteries with high power and long lifespan</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Dongxue; Bie, Xiaofei; Fu, Qiang; Dixon, Ditty; Bramnik, Natalia; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Fauth, Francois; Wei, Yingjin; Ehrenberg, Helmut; Chen, Gang; Du, Fei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">15888</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NCAOBW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2041-1723</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries operating at ambient temp. hold great promise for use in grid energy storage owing to their significant cost advantages.  However, challenges remain in the development of suitable electrode materials to enable long lifespan and high rate capability.  Here we report a sodium super-ionic conductor structured electrode, sodium vanadium titanium phosphate, which delivers a high specific capacity of 147 mA h g-1 at a rate of 0.1 C and excellent capacity retentions at high rates.  A sym. sodium-ion full cell demonstrates a superior rate capability with a specific capacity of about 49 mA h g-1 at 20 C rate and ultralong lifetime over 10,000 cycles.  Furthermore, in situ synchrotron diffraction and X-ray absorption spectroscopy measurement are carried out to unravel the underlying sodium storage mechanism and charge compensation behavior.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The surface of olivine NaFePO4 was modified with polythiophene (PTh) to develop a high-performance cathode material for use in Na-ion batteries.  The Rietveld refinement results of the prepd. material reveal that PTh-coated NaFePO4 belongs to a space group of Pnma with lattice parameters of a = 10.40656 Å, b = 6.22821 Å, and c = 4.94971 Å.  Uncoated NaFePO4 delivers a discharge capacity of 108 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 10 mA g-1 within a voltage range of 2.2-4.0 V.  Conversely, the PTh-coated NaFePO4 electrode exhibits significantly improved electrochem. performance, where it exhibits a discharge capacity of 142 mAh g-1 and a stable cycle life over 100 cycles, with a capacity retention of 94%.  The NaFePO4/PTh electrode also exhibits satisfactory performance at high current densities, and reversible capacities of 70 mAh g-1 at 150 mA g-1 and 42 mAh g-1 at 300 mA g-1 are obtained compared with negligible capacities without coating.  The related electrochem. reaction mechanism has been investigated using in situ X-ray absorption spectroscopy (XAS), which revealed a systematic change of Fe valence and reversible contraction/expansion of Fe-O octahedra upon desodiation/sodiation.  The ex situ X-ray diffraction (XRD) results suggest that the deintercalation in NaFePO4/PTh electrodes proceeds through a stable intermediate phase and the lattice parameters show a reversible contraction/expansion of unit cell during cycling.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref13" class="rightTabRefNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit13" data-doi="10.1149/1.1393348"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Stevens, D.                         rightTab-cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Direct atomic-scale confirmation of three-phase storage mechanism in Li4Ti5O12 anodes for room-temperature sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun Yang; Zhao Liang; Pan Huilin; Lu Xia; Gu Lin; Hu Yong-Sheng; Li Hong; Armand Michel; Ikuhara Yuichi; Chen Liquan; Huang Xuejie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),

    </div><div class="casAbstract">Room-temperature sodium-ion batteries attract increasing attention for large-scale energy storage applications in renewable energy and smart grid.  However, the development of suitable anode materials remains a challenging issue.  Here we demonstrate that the spinel Li4Ti5O12, well-known as a 'zero-strain' anode for lithium-ion batteries, can also store sodium, displaying an average storage voltage of 0.91 V.  With an appropriate binder, the Li4Ti5O12 electrode delivers a reversible capacity of 155 mAh g(-1) and presents the best cyclability among all reported oxide-based anode materials.  Density functional theory calculations predict a three-phase separation mechanism, 2Li4Ti5O12+6Na(+)+6e(-)↔Li7Ti5O12+Na6LiTi5O12, which has been confirmed through in situ synchrotron X-ray diffraction and advanced scanning transmission electron microscope imaging techniques.  The three-phase separation reaction has never been seen in any insertion electrode materials for lithium- or sodium-ion batteries. Herein, we report a facile synthesis method for nanosized V2O5/C composite cathodes and their electrochem. performance as well as energy storage mechanism.  The composite exhibits a discharge capacity of 255 mAh/g at a c.d. of 0.05 C, which surpasses that of previously reported layered oxide materials.  Furthermore, the electrode shows good rate capability, discharge capacity of 160 mAh/g at a c.d. of 1 C. Ex situ XRD result of the fully discharged state reveals the appearance of NaV2O5 as a major phase with minor Na2V2O5 phase.  Upon insertion of sodium into the array of parallel ladders of V2O5, it was confirmed that lattice parameter of c is increased by 9.09%, corresponding to the increase in the unit-cell vol. of 9.2%.  NEXAFS results suggest that the charge compensation during de/sodiation process accompanied by the reversible changes in the oxidn. state of vanadium (V4+ ↔ V5+).</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref30" class="rightTabRefNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit30" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.7b02480"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pei, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sheng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tan, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">An, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mai, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">VO2 Nanoflakes as the Cathode Material of Hybrid Magnesium–Lithium-Ion Batteries with High Energy Density</span>. <i>ACS Appl.         </div><div class="casAbstract">LiVO3 has been proposed as an appealing cathode material to substitute traditional capacity-limited cathodes for high-energy lithium-ion batteries.  However, just like other Li-V-O compds., the application of the LiVO3 cathode is restricted by its poor cycling stability and rate capability.  In this paper, we report nanoplate-stacked baguette-like LiVO3 by an in situ template method.  In this unique structure, the microsized baguette shape can help to inhibit the dissoln. of vanadium in comparison with nanosized LiVO3, and the stacked nanoplates can provide short diffusion pathways for lithium ions.  Benefiting from these advantages, this material can deliver a very high capacity of 275.6 mA-h/g with excellent cycling stability.  Moreover, a capacity of 156.1 mA-h/g can be obtained up to 4C (1200 mA/g).  The exceptional electrochem. performance suggests the use of nanoplate-stacked baguette-like LiVO3 as an alternative cathode material for high-energy lithium-ion batteries.  Particularly, the synthesis strategy demonstrated herein may be extended to fabricate other types of multifunctional vanadium-based compds. for energy storage.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref32" class="rightTabRefNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit32" data-doi="10.1021/nl504705z"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, Y.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">van Aken, P.                         rightTab-cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Alkaline earth metal vanadates as sodium-ion battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu Xiaoming; Niu Chaojiang; Wang Xuanpeng; Huang Lei; Wang Junhui; Pu Liting; Ren Wenhao; Shi Changwei; Meng Jiasheng; Mai Liqiang; Duan Manyi; Song Bo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">460</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">The abundance of sodium resources indicates the potential of sodium-ion batteries as emerging energy storage devices.  However, the practical application of sodium-ion batteries is hindered by the limited electrochemical performance of electrode materials, especially at the anode side.  Here, we identify alkaline earth metal vanadates as promising anodes for sodium-ion batteries.  The prepared calcium vanadate nanowires possess intrinsically high electronic conductivity (&gt; 100 S cm(-1)), small volume change (&lt; 10%), and a self-preserving effect, which results in a superior cycling and rate performance and an applicable reversible capacity (&gt; 300 mAh g(-1)), with an average voltage of ∼1.0 V.  The specific sodium-storage mechanism, beyond the conventional intercalation or conversion reaction, is demonstrated through in situ and ex situ characterizations and theoretical calculations.  This work explores alkaline earth metal vanadates for sodium-ion battery anodes and may open a direction for energy storage.The development of suitable anode materials is essential to advance sodium-ion battery technologies.  Here the authors report that alkaline earth metal vanadates are promising candidates due to the favorable electrochemical properties and interesting sodium-storage mechanism.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref37" class="rightTabRefNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit37" data-doi="10.1021/cm502268u"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chae, O.                         rightTab-cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Reversible Lithium Storage at Highly Populated Vacant Sites in an Amorphous Vanadium Pentoxide Electrode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chae, Oh B.; Kim, Jisun; Park, Inchul; Jeong, Hyejeong; Ku, Jun H.; Ryu, Ji Heon; Kang, Kisuk; Oh, Seung M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A V pentoxide electrode is prepd. in the amorphous form (a-V2O5), and its electrode performances are compared to those for its cryst. counterpart (c-V2O5).  The a-V2O5 electrode outperforms c-V2O5 in several ways.  First, it is free from irreversible phase transitions and Li trapping, which evolve in c-V2O5, probably due to the lack of interactions between the inserted Li+ ions/electrons and V2O5 matrix.  Second, the absence of Li trapping allows a reversible capacity amounting to &gt;600 mA-h g-1, which is larger than that given by c-V2O5.  Third, it shows an excellent rate property.  The notably high reversible capacity and rate capability seem to be due to Li storage at vacant sites that are ill-defined but numerous in a-V2O5, which Li+ ions can easily access.  However, irreversible capacity of a-V2O5 is appreciable in the 1st cycle due to a parasitic Li reaction with surface hydroxyl groups.  Treatment with BuLi can suppress the irreversible capacity by removing the surface hydroxyl groups.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref38" class="rightTabRefNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit38" data-doi="10.1107/s0909049505012719"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ravel, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Newville, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">ATHENA, ARTEMIS, HEPHAESTUS: data analysis for X-ray absorption spectroscopy using IFEFFIT</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A pseudo two-dimensional model (P2D) is presented that describes the effect of the structural properties of the pos. electrode on Li-ion cell performance during discharge.  The validation of the mono-modal model was done by using Doyle's expt. and results [C.M. Doyle, University of California, Berkeley (1995)].  A large increase or decrease in the porosity beyond a specific value led to a sharp change in the cell voltage curve and lower cell capacities.  The max. specific energy was obtained in the porosity range of 0.55, while the specific power still had a high value.  Furthermore, different particle size distribution models, including mono-modal, bi-modal and 3-particle models, were compared to each other.  The mono-modal model was the ideal state with the lowest total polarization.  The bi-modal and 3-particle models approached this ideal state when the vol. fraction of the smallest particles in their structures increased.  This structural arrangement in these models led to more uniform local c.d. distribution profiles resulting in a greater decrease in cell polarization.  Different discharge current densities were applied to different particle size distribution models, and the results showed that the particle size distribution has a greater effect at higher discharge current densities.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref46" class="rightTabRefNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit46" data-doi="10.1038/s41598-017-16711-9"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, Y.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ryu, K.-S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Study of the lithium diffusion properties and high rate performance of TiNb6O17 as an anode in lithium secondary battery</span>. <i>Sci. Rep.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>7</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">16617</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/s41598-017-16711-9</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Study of the lithium diffusion properties and high rate performance of TiNb6O17 as an anode in lithium secondary battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lee Yong-Seok; Ryu Kwang-Sun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Scientific reports</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">16617</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">TiNb6O17 and TiNb2O7 were synthesized using a solid-state method.  The techniques were used to assess the electrochemical performance and lithium diffusion kinetics of TiNb6O17 related to the unit cell volume with TiNb2O7.  The charge-discharge curves and cyclic voltammetry revealed TiNb6O17 to have a similar redox potential to TiNb2O7 as well as a high discharge capacity.  The rate performance of TiNb6O17 was measured using a rate capability test.  SSCV and EIS showed that TiNb6O17 had higher lithium diffusion coefficients during the charging.  From GITT, the lithium diffusion coefficients at the phase transition region showed the largest increase from TiNb2O7 to TiNb6O17.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref47" class="rightTabRefNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit47" data-doi="10.1063/1.2831484"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Backholm, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Georén, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Niklasson, G. A.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Determination of solid phase chemical diffusion coefficient and density of states by electrochemical methods: Application to iridium oxide-based thin films</span>. <i>J. Appl. Phys.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2008</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>103</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">023702</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1063/1.2831484</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Determination of solid phase chemical diffusion coefficient and density of states by electrochemical methods: Application to iridium oxide-based thin films</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Backholm, Jonas; Georen, Peter; Niklasson, Gunnar A.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Applied Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2008</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">103</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">023702/1-023702/10</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JAPIAU</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0021-8979</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Institute of Physics</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Potentiostatic intermittent titrn. technique (PITT) and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy (EIS) were studied as methods to det. solid phase chem. diffusion coeff. (D) and electronic d. of states (DOS).  These techniques were then applied to Ir oxide (IrOx) and Ir-Ta oxide (IrTaOx) thin films prepd. by sputter deposition.  The expts., performed in 1M propionic acid between -0.2 and 0.8 V vs. Ag/AgCl, showed effects of interfacial side reactions, whose contribution to the electrochem. response could be identified and cor. for in the case of PITT as well as EIS.  D is strongly underestimated when using PITT with the common Cottrell formalism, which follows from nonnegligible interfacial charge transfer and ohmic resistances.  EIS indicated an anomalous diffusion mechanism, and D is in the 10-11-10-10 cm2/s range for IrOx and IrTaOx.  Both PITT and EIS showed that the intercalated charge as a function of potential exhibits a shape that resembles the theor. DOS of cryst. Ir oxide, esp. for IrTaOx.  (c) 2008 American Institute of Physics.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref48" class="rightTabRefNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit48" data-doi="10.1039/c6ra06533c"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Niu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, C. M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Detailed investigation of a NaTi2(PO4)3 anode prepared by pyro-synthesis for Na-ion batteries</span>. <i>RSC Adv.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>6</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">45605</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">45611</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c6ra06533c</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Detailed investigation of a NaTi2(PO4)3 anode prepared by pyro-synthesis for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Niu, Yubin; Xu, Maowen; Zhang, Yan; Han, Jin; Wang, Yan; Li, Chang Ming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">51</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">45605-45611</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">RSCACL</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2046-2069</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">NaTi2(PO4)3 nanoparticles were synthesized by a facile polyol-assisted pyro-synthetic reaction.  The nitrogen sorption isotherm of the synthesized material shows a surface area of 110.787 m2 g-1, in comparison to 20.984 m2 g-1 for pristine material obtained by a solid state method.  Moreover, the as-prepd. material exhibits much higher capacity, better rate performance and lower electrochem. polarization, of which the excellent electrochem. performance is mainly attributed to uniform particle distribution, good structural stability, high sp. surface area, significantly enhanced diffusion coeff. and good cond.  Through systematic studies using a galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique (GITT) and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy (EIS) at different states of charge and discharge, the Na+ diffusion coeff. shows a min. value at the end of the two-phase region.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref49" class="rightTabRefNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit49" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2004.01.048"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ning, L. J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y. P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, S. B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rahm, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Holze, R.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Materials prepared for lithium ion batteries by mechanochemical methods</span>. <i>J. Power Sources</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2004</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>133</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">229</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">242</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2004.01.048</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref50" class="rightTabRefNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit50" data-doi="10.1021/ja310347x"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Darwiche, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Marino, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sougrati, M. T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fraisse, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Stievano, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Monconduit, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Better Cycling Performances of Bulk Sb in Na-Ion Batteries Compared to Li-Ion Systems: An Unexpected Electrochemical Mechanism</span>. <i>J. Am. Chem. Soc.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>134</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">20805</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">20811</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/ja310347x</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Better Cycling Performances of Bulk Sb in Na-Ion Batteries Compared to Li-Ion Systems: An Unexpected Electrochemical Mechanism</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Darwiche, Ali; Marino, Cyril; Sougrati, Moulay T.; Fraisse, Bernard; Stievano, Lorenzo; Monconduit, Laure</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">134</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">51</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">20805-20811</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pure micrometric antimony can be successfully used as neg. electrode material in Na-ion batteries, sustaining a capacity close to 600 mAh g-1 at a high rate with a Coulombic efficiency of 99 over 160 cycles, an extremely high capacity compared to any other compd. tested against both Li and Na.  The reaction mechanism with Na does not simply go through the alloying mechanism obsd. for Li where the intermediate species are those expected from the phase diagram.  In the case of Na, the intermediate phases are mostly amorphous and could not be precisely identified.  Surprisingly, it is evidenced that a competition takes place at the end of the discharge of the Sb/Na cell between the formation of the hexagonal and the cubic polymorphs of Na3Sb, the last being described in the literature as unstable at atm. pressure and only synthesized under high pressure (1-9 GPa).  In addn., fluoroethylene carbonate added to the electrolyte combined with an appropriate electrode formulation based on CM-cellulose, carbon black, and vapor ground carbon fibers seems to be determinant in the excellent performances of this material.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li></ul></div></div></div></div></article><div class="w-slide article__w-slide">

(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

<script nonce="93188881ef5754b8-SJC">
document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function () {
    const modalContainer = document.querySelector('.my-main-container');

    // Function to show the modal
    function showModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'flex';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'block';
    }

    // Function to hide the modal when the close button is clicked
    function hideModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'none';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'none';
    }

    // Hide the modal initially
    hideModal();

    // Function to handle clicks outside the modal
    function handleClickOutside(event) {
        // const modalContainer = document.querySelector(".my-main-container");
        // Check if the click target is not a child of the modal container
        if (!modalContainer.contains(event.target)) {
            hideModal();
        }
    }

    // Add a click event listener to the close button
    document
        .querySelector('.close-button')
        .addEventListener('click', hideModal);

    // Add a click event listener to the document to handle clicks outside the modal
    document.addEventListener('click', handleClickOutside);

    const screenHeight = window.innerHeight;
    function updateModalPosition() {
        const scrollY = window.scrollY;
        // console.log("scrollY= " + scrollY);
        // modalContainer.style.top = `${50 + scrollY}px`;
        modalContainer.style.top = `${scrollY + screenHeight / 2}px`;
        // console.log("new top= " + modalContainer.style.top);
    }

    // Update the modal position when the user scrolls
    window.addEventListener('scroll', updateModalPosition);

    // Initialize the modal position
    updateModalPosition();

    //---Cookie---
    // Function to set the cookie with a given name, value, and expiration time in days
    function setCookie(name, value, days) {
        var expires = '';
        if (days) {
            var date = new Date();
            date.setTime(date.getTime() + days * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000);
            expires = '; expires=' + date.toUTCString();
            console.log(expires + 'this is expires dateUTC');
        }
        document.cookie = name + '=' + (value || '') + expires + '; path=/';
        // console.log("document.cookie is: " + document.cookie);
    }

    if (!document.cookie.includes('modalAd')) {
        // Show Modal
        showModal();

        // Set the cookie with the name "modalAd", value "true", and expiration of 3 day
        setCookie('modalAd', 'true', 3);
    } else {
        hideModal();
    }
});

</script>

<script nonce="93188881ef5754b8-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage =
          "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

      function init() {
        setTimeout(function () {
          var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
          if (cookieExist) {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
            return false;
          } else {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
            gdprMessage();
          }
          //Events
          $("#closebtn").on("click", hideForm);

          //Handle submit
          $("#gdpr-message-btn").on("click", function (event) {
            handleClick();
          });

          // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
          // $(document).click(function(event) {
          // 	event.stopPropagation();
          //   console.log(event.target);
          //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
          //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
          //     $(this).off();
          //   }
          // });
          $("#gdpr-con-btn").click(function () {
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            hideForm();
          });
        }, time);
      }

      //Show the message
      function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $("#gdpr-message-modal").show();
      }

      function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
          //Submit the form
          //Hide form
          if ($(".gdpr_err")) {
            $(".gdpr_err").hide();
          }

          $("#gdpr-message-content");
          //If successful then...
          setCookie("gdpr", "true");
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
          //Show error message
          gdprErrorMessage();
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
      }

      function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
          return false;
        } else {
          errorStatus = true;
          $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
      }

      function validateEmail(email) {
        var re =
          /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
      }

      function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
      }

      function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + "=([^;]+)"));
        if (match) return match[1];
      }

      function hideForm() {
        //And set cookie
        $("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag("event", "GDPR Modal", {
          event_category: "Pubs GDPR",
          event_label: "GDPR Dismissal",
        });
      }

      return {
        init: init,
      };
    })();

  </script>
</p>

        <script nonce="93188881ef5754b8-SJC">
var currentJournal = "ACS Applied Materials &amp;amp; Interfaces";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>
